  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_835b5cee-7b1a-4355-952b-c8737f6290fc'
      });

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=to-ya-or-not-to-ya">to-ya-or-not-to-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=kat-s-book-reviews">kat-s-book-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3270188-kat-kennedy?shelf=ya-pnr-maddness">ya-pnr-maddness</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer388975182" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17412399226090373787">Whether or not you enjoy this book depends on what you were expect­ing to begin with. No Really. Look at that cover, reread the syn­op­sis and decide right now what you’re hop­ing from this book. Is it:<br/><br/>a) A dark, twisted retelling of Alice in Won­der­land with zom­bie creatures?<br/><br/>b) A high school melo­drama about ghost/zombies with no real Alice in Won­der­land connection.<br/><br/>If you thought B then good for you. Read this book. If you thought A then back the hell off now. This is not the book for you a</span>
  <span id="freeText17412399226090373787" style="display:none">Whether or not you enjoy this book depends on what you were expect­ing to begin with. No Really. Look at that cover, reread the syn­op­sis and decide right now what you’re hop­ing from this book. Is it:<br><br>a) A dark, twisted retelling of Alice in Won­der­land with zom­bie creatures?<br><br>b) A high school melo­drama about ghost/zombies with no real Alice in Won­der­land connection.<br><br>If you thought B then good for you. Read this book. If you thought A then back the hell off now. This is not the book for you and you will likely be disappointed.<br><br>I thought A. From the title and the vague syn­op­sis I believed that this would be an Alice going into zom­bieland and deal­ing with a dark, unset­tling, gory ver­sion of Won­der­land with many of the themes and sym­bol­ism from the orig­i­nal story mod­ern­ized and reimag­ined in this book. I thought this was going to be a book ver­sion of Amer­i­can McGee’s Alice.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380387209i/747171._SX540_.jpg" alt="Dark Alice" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now, just to make it clear. It’s not a book or author’s fault if that book was not what the reader imag­ined. But I do think the title and syn­op­sis is mis­lead­ing con­sid­er­ing a num­ber of peo­ple, myself included are prob­a­bly a lit­tle con­fused about what this actu­ally is. The syn­op­sis is vague, men­tion­ing only revenge and mon­sters and a bad boy.<br><br>So let’s clear this up. This is what Alice in Zom­bieland is:<br><br>Alice’s entire fam­ily die in a car crash. Her father, who always believed in zom­bies (they aren’t phys­i­cal zom­bies. They’re incor­po­real, evil spir­its that attack and eat your soul) is eaten. Alice, orphaned, goes to a new school where stu­dents act strangely. In par­tic­u­lar, a stu­dent name Cole who is all badass and secre­tive. Instalove, love tri­an­gles, spe­cial girl with spe­cial pow­ers later, blah blah blah THAT is the story.<br><br>In fact it felt, while read­ing, that the Alice in Won­der­land ele­ments were shooed in at the last minute and didn’t feel as though they were native or even rel­e­vant to the story. Cer­tainly, whilst the author links to a cou­ple of small, incon­se­quen­tial details like the white rab­bit and the Cheshire cat, none of the themes of Alice seemed touched upon or incor­po­rated into the story as a whole. Which is a shame because the com­ing of age in a strange and crazy world that every­one thinks is nor­mal theme would have worked so extremely well IN A YOUNG ADULT NOVEL ABOUT ZOMBIES!<br><br>But instead of talk­ing about what I wanted the book to be – what is the actual book like? Well, just not for me. Showal­ter is tran­si­tion­ing from adult para­nor­mal romance to YA and I don’t think it was suc­cess­ful. She built Cole off the foun­da­tion of a roman­ti­cized Alpha male – if that’s your thing fine, but I think the effect is lost when the audi­ence is reminded that this is a six­teen year old boy. Like when they’re at the club and intim­i­dat­ing grown men away from the girls by growl­ing. Yeah…<br><br>Alice is a rea­son­able char­ac­ter, though not one I had a great deal of inter­est in. She sim­ply capit­u­lated too much to Cole’s cave­man­ish ten­den­cies to keep my inter­est. The gen­eral cast is alright but it is quite siz­able and bur­dens the plot with a great deal of what felt like unnec­es­sary pos­tur­ing and con­vers­ing over things the audi­ence already knows.<br><br>I some­what expected bet­ter from the writ­ing con­sid­er­ing this is far from Showalter’s debut novel. The action scenes did not feel well real­ized and the final bat­tle was amaz­ingly short and anti­cli­matic. There was a focus on the romance. To be fair, it’s by no means a single-minded focus, sim­ply too much for me con­sid­er­ing I had no invest­ment in their rela­tion­ship to begin with. Instalove is not a plot device that I like. I never felt that I cham­pi­oned the rela­tion­ship between these two char­ac­ters because it never seemed to me that they had any chem­istry to begin with or even liked each other – at all.<br><br>My basic advice before buy­ing this book would be to read as many reviews of it as you can by peo­ple whose opin­ion you trust, decide if it is some­thing that’s going to appeal to you and read the sam­ple online before you purchase.<br><br>Basi­cally, would it have been too hard to have a story where Alice and the Mad Hat­ter throw down in a knife fight? Really, guys? REALLY?!</span>
  <a data-text-id="17412399226090373787" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16357780119684086448" style="display:none">I absolutely love this book. <span id="freeTextContainer8719230979844617463">Going into this I had a really good feeling that I wouldn't like it and I was right. First problem is I don't like zombies (which is obviously a personal preference thing), second problem is the fact that this is just a superficial high school drama, and the third and biggest problem for me is the fact that this is not a damn Alice in Wonderland retelling. People had warned me about that going in but I thought I'd at least get something considering the title of this and it's sequels but NOPE I w</span>
  <span id="freeText8719230979844617463" style="display:none">Going into this I had a really good feeling that I wouldn't like it and I was right. First problem is I don't like zombies (which is obviously a personal preference thing), second problem is the fact that this is just a superficial high school drama, and the third and biggest problem for me is the fact that this is not a damn Alice in Wonderland retelling. People had warned me about that going in but I thought I'd at least get something considering the title of this and it's sequels but NOPE I was lied to. What shoddy false advertisement. Overall this just made me feel annoyed.</span>

<div id="review_278503568" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/278503568" />
    <a title="shady boots" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4972138-shady-boots"><img alt="shady boots" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592459241p2/4972138.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/278503568?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="shady boots" class="user" itemprop="url" name="shady boots" href="/user/show/4972138-shady-boots">shady boots</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=covergasm">covergasm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=get-that-thing-away-from-me">get-that-thing-away-from-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=unoriginal">unoriginal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=stupid-girls">stupid-girls</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=why-do-people-like-this-shit">why-do-people-like-this-shit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=hot-mess">hot-mess</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4972138-shady-boots?shelf=dont-understand-why-its-hyped">dont-understand-why-its-hyped</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer278503568" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11697829342894292746">As you can see this is another DNF review, because I can only take so much torture, and reading this was overkill. I made it about 120-something pages, and then I reached my breaking point.<br/><br/><b>What I Oh So Desperately Wanted:</b> An awesome, zombiefied <i>Alice in Wonderland</i> retelling with lots of action.<br/><br/><b>What I Got:</b> Crappy, unoriginal, stereotypical teen melodrama.<br/><br/>So we have Alice, a girl who's dad is claimed to be psycho cause he sees these "monsters". And then her whole family gets killed in a car crash </span>
  <span id="freeText11697829342894292746" style="display:none">As you can see this is another DNF review, because I can only take so much torture, and reading this was overkill. I made it about 120-something pages, and then I reached my breaking point.<br><br><b>What I Oh So Desperately Wanted:</b> An awesome, zombiefied <i>Alice in Wonderland</i> retelling with lots of action.<br><br><b>What I Got:</b> Crappy, unoriginal, stereotypical teen melodrama.<br><br>So we have Alice, a girl who's dad is claimed to be psycho cause he sees these "monsters". And then her whole family gets killed in a car crash with her in it and she mysteriously survives (of course, doesn't sound familiar or unoriginal at all whatsoever). She gets moved into a new school and meets this bad boy who's, and I quote, "serial killer-esque" and she immediately fantasizes about him when they first lock eyes (not kidding).<br><br>Okay. So let's start with Cole.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/383186.gif" height="200" width="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Where do I even begin?<br><br>He's the leader of the bad boys in the school. He's extremely gorgeous and muscular with violet eyes and his ex-girlfriend is the bitchy and perfect queen of the school.<br><br>Cole is like Patch, Daniel and even friggin <i>Daemon</i>, the father of all YA pricks, all rolled into one. He scowls at Ali when they first meet, and even <i>snaps his teeth</i> at her. What the hell? <br><br>I stopped reading this book by the time Cole became this extremely controlling prick all of a sudden, even to the point of <i>demanding</i> Ali to give him her number. I'm not kidding, folks. I mean, I've read about some pretty controlling YA heroes, but he just takes it to a whole nother level. A <i>Christian Grey</i> level.<br><br>The insta-lust was ridiculous. Not five seconds after Ali first locks eyes with him, she's fantasizing about kissing him. <i>Literally</i>. There's, like, whole paragraphs of a makeout scene, all in her head. And then all she thinks about is Cole Cole Cole and how muscular and hot he is.<br><br>I stopped liking Ali right about the time she meets Cole. She was so pathetic in front of him, and the fact that after they meet Cole is pretty much the only thing in her mind didn't help at all.<br><br>There's also Ali's annoying friend, Kat. She meets her at the hospital cause Kat's mom works there and all she does is talk and talk and gossip and it's so friggin annoying that I wanted to reach into the pages of the book just to slap the shit outta her.<br><br>What I'm most most <i>most</i> sad about is of course the faux <i>Alice in Wonderland</i> retelling. The title and the cover (<i>Off with their heads.</i>) and even the name of the series, <i>White Rabbit Chronicles</i>, made me think that this would be an honest-to-god <i>Alice</i> retelling. But no. I guess that was just some method to lure all those fairytale-retelling fanatics out there to pick this book up.<br><br>If you are one of those fanatics, as am I, I will tell you this now: <b>This is not an <i>Alice</i> retelling. Save yourselves! D:</b> If you want a good, <i>real</i> YA <i>Alice</i> retelling, try <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12558285.Splintered__Splintered___1_" title="Splintered (Splintered, #1) by A.G. Howard" rel="nofollow noopener">Splintered</a> by A.G. Howard, which I adored. &lt;3<br><br>The 120-something pages I read were absolute torture, and there was nothing about this book that made me want to continue reading. It had numerous chances and they were all blown to pieces. Overall, this was your average teen melodrama story with some ghosts and zombies sprinkled onto it. Oh, and <i>Alice in Wonderland</i> references, for whatever reason.<br><br>In short, avoid this book at all costs. I definitely learned my lesson. ._. I should have listened to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/388975182" rel="nofollow noopener">Kat Kennedy's review</a> and took it as a warning.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11697829342894292746" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=own">own</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer307052146" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12594325502728742431">OFF WITH HER HEAD!!<br/><br/>Alice in Wonderland with zombies? Not so much. Creative zombie ghosts lore (… you heard me. Zombie. Ghosts) with great humor and charming characters? Definitely! <br/><br/>Despite the title, Alice in Zombieland really has nothing much to do with Alice in Wonderland. There may be some scattered references, but it's really a unique story all on its own. While some may be disappointed, I wasn't terribly familiar with the specifics of the classic tale, so I found myself having a lot of fun </span>
  <span id="freeText12594325502728742431" style="display:none">OFF WITH HER HEAD!!<br><br>Alice in Wonderland with zombies? Not so much. Creative zombie ghosts lore (… you heard me. Zombie. Ghosts) with great humor and charming characters? Definitely! <br><br>Despite the title, Alice in Zombieland really has nothing much to do with Alice in Wonderland. There may be some scattered references, but it's really a unique story all on its own. While some may be disappointed, I wasn't terribly familiar with the specifics of the classic tale, so I found myself having a lot of fun with this non-retelling. Really, all I need are zombies. Wouldn't every fairy tale be much more interesting with zombies? I think so! :D<br><br>Charming, this book absolutely is! Which is funny to say for a zombie book. Ali leads this story with a tough, head held high attitude; she's feisty with a great sense of humor that I got a kick out of. Then we have her friend Kat who really completes the show. Spunky, wild, and lots of fun, Kat is a fabulous girl who I came to adore. She has a very attractive confidence and qualities that everyone would want in a best friend. Plus, she has secrets of her own that add depth to the story. And of course, we have boys; most prominently - Cole. The leader of the bad boys, Cole is sexy and fierce with a mysterious agenda of his own, and Ali hopes she won't regret putting her trust into him. His irksome attitude towards Ali motivates some pretty humoristic dialogue/banter between them; their opinions tend to clash more than harmonize. Let's just say, the tension between them is just as adorable as it is frustrating. While the romance isn't my favorite aspect of this novel--the constant back and forth between them <i>can</i> get a little exasperating--they do have great chemistry to work with. <br><br>Set at the perfect pace, the plot is centered around these zombies that are not your run of the mill zombies, these exist in the spirit world. While I love the traditional zombie, and at first I wasn't sure how I would enjoy this bizarre re-imagining, it's simply too creative to not have me fascinated by it all. I was a little confused with the specifics, however: Who can see them and who they can hurt exactly, is not made very clear. But we still have time to get into these details. Zombies: meet the Hazmats, a villainous company looking to experiment on your rotted ghost person! And their intentions? Duh duh duuuuuh! The Hazmats add a great mysterious edge to the plot which also opens up intriguing possibilities for its sequel. All of this adds up to a refreshingly unique little paranormal romance.<br><br>There is humor, there are zombies, there are witty characters, even the chapter titles are hilarious! What else do you need? Oh, and the sequel is called "Through the Zombie Glass". Win? Yes! Yes it does!<br><br>--<br><i>An advance copy was provided by the publisher for review.</i><br><br>For more of my reviews, visit my blog at <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Xpresso Reads</a> <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380346185i/700655.png" width="380" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9187796554431694331"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420429845ra/13223235.gif' width='500' height='245' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Alice in Zombieland tells the story of Alice, who goes by Ali, and her life ends up being a non-stop zombie hunt. Alice is a sixteen years old girl, pretty ordinary, except that she's not. She has a pretty regular mother, an absolutely funny and charming little sister and a "crazy" father. She's always lived with her father rules:<br/><b>Never go out at night. <br/>Never to venture into a cemetery. <br/>And never, under any circumstances, to trust someone who wants you to do either.</b><br/>But we all have our time and af</span>
  <span id="freeText9187796554431694331" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420429845ra/13223235.gif" width="500" height="245" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Alice in Zombieland tells the story of Alice, who goes by Ali, and her life ends up being a non-stop zombie hunt. Alice is a sixteen years old girl, pretty ordinary, except that she's not. She has a pretty regular mother, an absolutely funny and charming little sister and a "crazy" father. She's always lived with her father rules:<br><b>Never go out at night. <br>Never to venture into a cemetery. <br>And never, under any circumstances, to trust someone who wants you to do either.</b><br>But we all have our time and after all the family went to Alice's sister performance as a birthday present to Alice, there comes this accident where everyone dies, except Alice and what she sees change her already changed life. Zombies roaming around, eating her dad. Alice's life is never the same and after her family dies she's forced to move in with her grandparents, not knowing what was going to happen. She's made some friends and meets the bad boys, but this particular violet eyed guy holds her attention and BAMM, she has a vision of the two of them kissing. She's not sure how that happened but a terrible feeling is suffocating her. Zombies are hunting her down and she's got no idea in what rabbit hole she got herself into.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423200064ra/13597104.gif" width="500" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I really have to say I loved this book <i>a lot</i>. Gena is one of my favorite writers and this book was so much fun I couldn't put it down! I fell in love with Alice and Kat! <br>I've wanted to pick up this book for a while now but I just didn't. See, zombies aren't really my thing. Never read so much about them to be honest, but boy didn't I love this book.<br><br>Call it a retelling isn't exactly right, though. I'll call it an inspired on book, but that doesn't mean it isn't enjoyable at all, it was pretty cool.<br><br>Alice was such a joy to read. She's fierce, lovely, funny, loyal, stubborn, she doesn't let anyone bosses her around, strong... she's just awesome, okay?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380401795ra/780231.gif" width="499" height="232" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And you gotta love Kat. I mean <i>“Besides, life’s too short to pretend and play games like that. I want to spend my time hanging out with people who make me feel good about myself. People who make me happy.”</i> That girl so damn loyal and funny and I wanna be her friend.<br><br>Overall, I liked all the girls in this book. Truly. They were different and they all gave something to the book. Do I need to say I absolutely loved Alice again? She's so bad-ass just by being herself. And then she kills zombies on top of that.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423200064ra/13597105.gif" width="483" height="281" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now, the boys didn't make that much of a impression to me, and I have to say I only started liking Cole about 5 chapters before the end, but I did like him a lot. He was so cute, actually. And Frosty, (lol, I loved the nicknames) was also really cute. I mean, the boys were alright but in my opinion, they were eclipsed by the girls and I know it's not a competition, but what can I do? Loved 'em all.<br><br>I'm so intrigued, though.<br>Why Alice has those zombie-like thoughts? <i>maim... kill... destroy...</i>?<br>She's one hell of a special slayer but why does she have does abilities?<br>What the hell with those shared visions with Cole?<br><br>I need to read the next book like now!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1423200064ra/13597106.gif" width="500" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Gena's books are always so funny. Man, she just got me in the mood!<br><br></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_371306557" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/371306557" />
    <a title="Navdha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5491368-navdha"><img alt="Navdha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1348070166p2/5491368.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/371306557?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Navdha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Navdha" href="/user/show/5491368-navdha">Navdha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5491368-navdha?shelf=cough-masochism-cough">cough-masochism-cough</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5491368-navdha?shelf=idon-tlikethatcharacter">idon-tlikethatcharacter</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5491368-navdha?shelf=shameful-shelf-of-meh">shameful-shelf-of-meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5491368-navdha?shelf=kill-them-or-kill-me">kill-them-or-kill-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5491368-navdha?shelf=why-oh-why">why-oh-why</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5491368-navdha?shelf=ummm-really">ummm-really</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5491368-navdha?shelf=yay-it-s-over">yay-it-s-over</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5491368-navdha?shelf=i-don-t-know-if-i-can">i-don-t-know-if-i-can</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5491368-navdha?shelf=not-very-happy">not-very-happy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5491368-navdha?shelf=predictable">predictable</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer371306557" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2402596045188636891">Does the title <i>Alice in Zombieland</i> along with the intriguing synopsis and lovely cover has you convinced that you <i>have</i> to read this book? <br/><br/>No? Never mind.<br/><br/>But if your answer is ‘Yes’, then you need to ask yourself this:<br/><br/>Are you expecting to find a gory, engrossing, retelling of Alice in Wonderland with zombie <s>goodness</s> putridness? <br/><br/>No? Okay.<br/>So far so good.<br/><br/>Are you prepared to go through the same overused insta-lust bullshit between the main characters with hardly any explanations or focus on the plot </span>
  <span id="freeText2402596045188636891" style="display:none">Does the title <i>Alice in Zombieland</i> along with the intriguing synopsis and lovely cover has you convinced that you <i>have</i> to read this book? <br><br>No? Never mind.<br><br>But if your answer is ‘Yes’, then you need to ask yourself this:<br><br>Are you expecting to find a gory, engrossing, retelling of Alice in Wonderland with zombie <s>goodness</s> putridness? <br><br>No? Okay.<br>So far so good.<br><br>Are you prepared to go through the same overused insta-lust bullshit between the main characters with hardly any explanations or focus on the plot which is fairly predictable?<br><br>No? You lucky bastard! <br><br>But if it’s a still a yes, I <i>really</i> hope you like it. Or if you are somewhat skeptical then you can continue reading my review and then decide for yourself. <br><br>You know, the rating along with a good synopsis is enough to make me want to read a book. Gena Showalter impressed me with her work in the <i>Intertwined</i> series and her work in <i>Lords of the Underworld</i> (the first 3-4 books) was good for my taste. So obviously I wanted to see her take on the Young-Adult genre but I’m really disappointed to add that her two books I read this year ended up with nothing but a 1-star rating from me. <br><br>The prologue and I hit it off instantly. I didn’t know what to expect from this book because of the mixed ratings I had come across but I was ready to be a little disappointed. What I <b>wasn’t</b> ready for was to find the characters so unbearably aggravating that I had to stop reading for long intervals and then had to drag myself to finish it. <br>The plot, actually, is very promising. I like reading macabre zombie tales and even though you don’t find the traditional zombies here, the new type of zombies that Showalter introduced were just as savage and even though they weren’t the shambling types, their role in the story was the least disappointing <s>Okay, I admit, I wanted them screaming “BWWAAAIIINNNSSS”…but oh well</s>.<br><br>Anyways, let’s talk about the actual storyline for a while before I start seeing red thinking about those irritating characters, hmm?<br><br>We have Alice Bell, a 16-year old, as our protagonist who has a lunatic for a father, a submissive, loving woman for a mother and a larger than life 8-year old for a sister. She despises her father for all his crazy talks of monsters and for forcing a daily lockdown of the entire family before sunset. One tragic night she loses her entire family to a car-crash and that’s what it takes for her to realize that her father wasn’t crazy after all. <br><br>The beginning itself started giving me hints about Meyer’s involvement. Like how the girl changes city/school, gets instantly attracted to the hot bad boy who’s to be avoided according to all her newly made girlfriends, add in the staring game across lunch tables in cafeteria along with getting lost in each other’s eyes (however in this case Showalter makes it too literal because the two of them actually lose all sense of reality on eye contact) and you have the clichéd failed romance for the story. Follow this up with guy telling girl not to get involved, girl telling guy he doesn’t scare her off when he actually does, guy not being able to stay away from girl and ordering her around by asking her not to see a certain other guy friend who is the potential love-interest for a triangle in sequels, girl wanting the guy real bad and *dun dun dun* getting involved so deep that she has to lie to her family (which as we all know ends up badly) and there, you have the story! Oh just put in more bitchiness from every other character, a zombie sighting or fighting here and there, girl getting close to dying but surviving (shocker.. *rolls eyes*) and voila, you have the disaster recipe for what-not-to-do in a zombie book!<br><br>To top it all off, there is some more head-desking, face-palming and general nuisance that the book makes you go through with the predictability, unappealing characters, lack of explanation and an anticlimactic ending, that you’d find yourself with an expression like this:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/523641.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Speaking of lack of explanations, I feel like Showalter wasted such a brilliant concept by revealing next to nothing about how the zombies came into being or why Alice was so very “speshul” in fighting them off or why <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[her father couldn’t resist the evil when her mother did when he was more prepared <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> or why <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Emma got to be the witness and not her mother <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. There was also that discrepancy in the last fighting scene that has been bothering me. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Ali’s father was bound by the blood line noose on his neck right? So how could he devour Haun? Did he somehow get rid of the noose?  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> What do you have to say for yourself, dear author? And since we’re on the topic of what’s bothering me, let’s talk about Kat, Showalter. She was obnoxious, egotistical, and got on my nerves. If you were trying to give Ali a bff, couldn’t she be hilarious without being annoying? Who the hell meets you on day one and shares all their summer secrets in a minute? Okay, forget that, can you tell me why that little surprise? Was it meant for the readers to sympathize with her? Guess what, I don’t care. It just felt like a useless thing to do or maybe it was meant as a plot device to make us suspicious of her or something? Amirite?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380384429ra/742915.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Well, now about the ending. I shouldn’t have expected anything better after reading only two fight scenes with no sense of looming danger or anticipation that a zombie book makes you crave for, but seriously, the ending could’ve been so much better. I admit that I hadn’t expected <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Dr. Wight  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> on the other team, but again it failed to leave an impression.<br><br>Umm…after so much beating around the bush I think I can’t avoid talking about what made me the most peevish about this book, right? <br>Thought so. <br>So shall I start <s>ranting</s> talking about Ali and Cole? <br><br>Okay…*cracks knuckles*<br><br>Ali, where should I even begin? You know I felt real bad for your loss and your family’s death must have been quite traumatic. I know you needed something to make you feel less guilty and take your mind off things for a while. I really wish lusting for the bad-boy who was actually a manipulative, condescending jerk wasn’t your way of dealing. Hadn’t you been mad on your dad for ordering you to stay home and not letting you live life like a normal teenager? How could you find Cole’s bossiness charming then? Was it the violet eyes? I understand how that along with his sexiness would have made your mouth water but really girl, doesn’t a personality count? You mouthed him off a couple of times but secretly thinking thoughts like, “Please want me!” was what made me want to slam your head against the wall. I hope you realize that you getting bitten by zombies every time gave me a sense of peace. Also, your bitchiness wasn’t warranted most of the times. In the end all I have to say to you is:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380384429ra/742916.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Cole…Dude, you were what? 16? I understand that your father having knowledge on everything zombie gave you a sense of superiority or whatever, but did that give you a right to order around all your friends and treat them like your minions? Someone had to take the lead, it was necessary, but who left you in charge? You know what, I don’t entirely blame you. I blame the others who succumbed to your alpha-male role. I don’t hate you but every time you spoke, I just wanted to say:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380372768ra/726134.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I don’t care for all the other zombie slayers, I just don’t. Frosty was a whipped puppy on Kat’s leash, McKenzie was..okay, I think. She was jealous and clingy in the beginning but she didn’t bother me. The others like Trina, Bronx, Reeve etc. etc. made no difference to me with their existence. Also, I would have liked an explanation for Cole and Ali’s connection but needless to say, I didn’t get one.<br><br>Yeah, I’m done. Did I make you suffer much? Sorry. <br>I feel exhausted too after writing this review *cough *just as I was exhausted after finishing off the book*cough*. My rating makes it quite clear that I won’t be looking forward to any sequels. If I do, blame it on being a masochistic lion. <br>*snickers* See what I did there? <br>*sigh*<br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="2402596045188636891" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_309394009" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/309394009" />
    <a title="Kaylee Magic" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8098000-kaylee-magic"><img alt="Kaylee Magic" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1331164018p2/8098000.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/309394009?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaylee Magic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaylee Magic" href="/user/show/8098000-kaylee-magic">Kaylee Magic</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8098000-kaylee-magic?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer309394009" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6642521799039911254"><b>LOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOL!</b> Sweet Jesus, Ali is not your typical sit-back-and-take-it heroine -- she's wild for a girl who looks like a doll, and I SERIOUSLY LOVE THAT. Go kick some invisible zombie butt, Ali! (: ♥<br/><br/>-----<br/><br/><b>
  <i>Alice in Zombieland<i></i></i>
</b> is, quite frankly, not what I was expecting. It's BETTER. It ROCKS. It totally KICKED ASS, which I guess should've been expected of a Gena Showalter book incorporating zombies into my favourite childhood story. I always used to want to go to Wonderland</span>
  <span id="freeText6642521799039911254" style="display:none"><b>LOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOOL!</b> Sweet Jesus, Ali is not your typical sit-back-and-take-it heroine -- she's wild for a girl who looks like a doll, and I SERIOUSLY LOVE THAT. Go kick some invisible zombie butt, Ali! (: ♥<br /><br />-----<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Alice in Zombieland<i></i></i>
</b> is, quite frankly, not what I was expecting. It's BETTER. It ROCKS. It totally KICKED ASS, which I guess should've been expected of a Gena Showalter book incorporating zombies into my favourite childhood story. I always used to want to go to Wonderland before, but screw that now -- one ticket to the kick-ass world of Alice's Zombieland, please! <br /><br />This book starts off with a bang -- and I mean that literally. Ali's crazy dad, her adorable little sister, and her loving mother are all taken away from her in an instant where she learns that maybe her certifiable father wasn't so insane after all. Then she moves in with her grandparents, becomes BFFs with the hilariously amazing Kat (BEST BEST FRIEND EVER, NO JOKES), and meets Cole. <br /><br />Now this is where I fell in love. <br /><br />Cole is the leader of the school gang, a total badass, and extremely irritating to Ali -- especially when she realizes that his gang kills zombies instead of act broody without reason. Except these zombies aren't like what you'd expect. They're invisible to those who can't see them (like Ali couldn't before the accident), so there are only a select few who are equipped to fight them. He proves his worth a million times when he kills zombies, protects Ali, and puts up with her stubborn streaks like a guy with a gold medal in the PERFECT BOOK BOYFRIEND category. <br /><br />(And I know that many people find possessiveness unattractive in a male protagonist, but I LOVED how protective he was of Ali! You could easily see how much he didn't want her hurt, how much he wanted to protect her -- yet at the same time, he couldn't exactly deny her the chance to fight the monsters that murdered her family. Especially after she proved that she was ass-kickingly worthy of being the heroine of this novel, too. They were a perfect, sizzling, and amazing duo!)<br /><br />What I love about Ali is that she wants to help out almost immediately. She takes the risk of learning to sword-fight and hunt like any self-respecting heroine would -- even when she faces with death more than her fair share of times. <br /><br />What I love even MORE about Ali is her snark. Seriously. I think ALL of my favourite characters possess hilarious snark of some kind, and Ali has definitely got some of the funniest wisecracks in book history! <br /><br />-----<br /><br /><b>Kaylee's Conclusion...</b><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Alice in Zombieland</i>
</b> is A HUNDRED out of A HUNDRED shades of awesome, and FIVE out of FIVE shining stars of rewarding greatness. The beautifully fitting cover, the sexy yet sweet romance, and the powerful storyline full of many twists and turns make it a book that I feel EVERYONE needs to own! <br /><br />So what's stopping you? I want no excuses -- this book is a MUST on your buy lists for this fall! (: <br /><br />-----<br /><br /><b>TEASER:</b><br /><br /><i>Cole cupped my cheeks and brought my gaze back to him. "Why wouldn't I dance?" <br /><br />Uh, maybe because at first glance he looked like he ate puppies for breakfast and kittens for lunch? As for what he enjoyed having for dinner -- that couldn't be discussed in polite company.<br /><br />"Because you think it's dumb?" The words emerged as a question rather than the statement I'd meant them to be. <br /><br />"Something that allows a guy to put his hands all over a girl isn't dumb. It's genius."</i><br /><br />(quoted from the ARC)</span>
  <a data-text-id="6642521799039911254" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_421629693" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/421629693" />
    <a title="Katy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4572741-katy"><img alt="Katy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365039295p2/4572741.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/421629693?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katy" href="/user/show/4572741-katy">Katy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer421629693" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12386260145868746983">My Goodread friends have either really, really liked this book or really, really hated it. Now, I know why, and I have so many things to say about it - and not good ones.<br/><br/>First of all, I thought this book was going to be a parody of Alice in Wonderland or have some kind of parallelism or allusion to it, but the only things that lined up were a character named Alice and the mention of a white rabbit - in this book, it was the stupid clouds. So yeah, <b>
  <u>not much correlation to Alice in Wonderland.</u>
</b></span>
  <span id="freeText12386260145868746983" style="display:none">My Goodread friends have either really, really liked this book or really, really hated it. Now, I know why, and I have so many things to say about it - and not good ones.<br /><br />First of all, I thought this book was going to be a parody of Alice in Wonderland or have some kind of parallelism or allusion to it, but the only things that lined up were a character named Alice and the mention of a white rabbit - in this book, it was the stupid clouds. So yeah, <b>
  <u>not much correlation to Alice in Wonderland.</u>
</b><br /><br />Now where to go from here. <b>
  <u>This book was like watching a scary movie</u>
</b> where the characters are just heading towards trouble, and you're yelling, "Stop! Don't go any further! Turn back!" Yet, they still run straight into it, KNOWING nothing good can come out of it. In fact, Alice even referred to it as a scary movie. Why would go you go outside Alice? Please, tell me why? Stop! Abort! Abort!<br /><br /><b>
  <u>And the concept had potential, but nothing was ever explained.</u>
</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I just KNEW the "he" was her father. But if he was so adamant about being against them in the first place, why couldn't he fight them off? Why does Emma get to "come back" and help Alice? What's so special about Alice? Is it hereditary? Why can she make the light? The book mentioned a theory about a disease, and in the end, Alice said she has her suspicions. But what was it, and how does it fit in this story? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I know that Showalter plans to keep things for the sequel, but a book is incomplete when you don't even BEGIN to explain things.<br /><br />On a side note, <b>
  <u>I'm not opposed to instalove, but in this book, it was just downright ridiculous and corny.</u>
</b> The meeting of the eyes and immediately physical effects, the tunnel-visions, all of it. And <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[you never even find out WHY they are have the visions. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And the hot-cold relationship that they have? <b>
  <u>I'm all for bickering that gets you a bit riled up, but in this book, it was just annoying</u>
</b> because they were such an ass/bitch, and it was built on drama, not chemistry. And while Alice tells Cole to go away, she's silently praying, "Please. Want me." Ugh! Their conversations were either frustrating or sickeningly corny.<br /><br />Come to think of it, the whole book was pretty irritating to read. I think <b>
  <u>Showalter tried TOO hard to make this book "smart" if you know what I mean.</u>
</b> I was overloaded with the "Pretty Kitty" and "Mad Dog" or play on words like "pain in the neck" when referring to the sword knick. Try answering someone asking you how you're doing with a "I'm so good, I should be illegal." Too much. Just too much.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>There were annoying characters.</u>
</b> All of them were, but the two I could not stand were Alice and Kat. Alice was such a bitch. I understand being sassy and being a smart-mouth, but her character was written to the point where she was just snarky and downright rude. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Especially when it came to Justin before she even knew he was on the other team. And after the party, she screwed up by leaving him, and she wanted answers from him, yet her comments to him were just hurtful and nasty. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />And Kat? Who goes and tells someone they just met all about their dramatic relationship and sex life? She's dramatic and obnoxious. She's nosy and interfering. And her attempt to be such a badass was irritating. And what was up with her surprise? Can we be more cliche? Why? Why did you have to do that? Sometimes, annoying best friends can be written to where they are charming, but Kat was just too much.<br /><br />I know Showalter is a great writer, and I respect her and her works. But with this one, I just couldn't. <b>
  <u>I didn't just "not like" this book. I found it irritating and just really, really bad - and for me, it wasn't a "so bad it was good" type of book.</u>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="12386260145868746983" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_361668631" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Sarah Elizabeth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7591340-sarah-elizabeth"><img alt="Sarah Elizabeth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1328957304p2/7591340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer15902251723407937791">I was obviously expecting too much from this book, because boy was I disappointed.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425237342ra/13865996.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Alice was an okay character, I felt sorry for her because of the way she lost her whole family, and the way she blamed herself for it. It must have been really hard for her to find herself so alone, and to have to deal with the knowledge that the monsters her father raved about were actually real!<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425237342i/13865997._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The storyline in this revolved around Alice learning to fight zombies, and it got old real quick. I got bored. I felt li</span>
  <span id="freeText15902251723407937791" style="display:none">I was obviously expecting too much from this book, because boy was I disappointed.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425237342ra/13865996.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Alice was an okay character, I felt sorry for her because of the way she lost her whole family, and the way she blamed herself for it. It must have been really hard for her to find herself so alone, and to have to deal with the knowledge that the monsters her father raved about were actually real!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425237342i/13865997._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The storyline in this revolved around Alice learning to fight zombies, and it got old real quick. I got bored. I felt like half the book was info-dump after info-dump, and I didn’t really care for the insta-love romance either. I mean really?<br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425237342ra/13865998.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The ending to this did save this book for me a bit. At around the 90% mark it actually got interesting. It didn’t last for long though. Can’t say I’m desperate to read the next one. Just another example of not buying the sequel before you read the first one Sarah.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425237342ra/13865999.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>6 out of 10<br></span>

<div id="review_364517471" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/364517471" />
    <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library"><img alt="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350750103p2/4551536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/364517471?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maja (The Nocturnal Library)" href="/user/show/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library">Maja (The Nocturnal Library)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=cover-lust">cover-lust</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=role-models">role-models</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=reviewed-in-2012">reviewed-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=arc-2012">arc-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=zombies-zombies-everywhere">zombies-zombies-everywhere</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=own-a-dtb">own-a-dtb</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4551536-maja-the-nocturnal-library?shelf=mira-ink">mira-ink</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer364517471" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3560949713556867705">I’m sure you’ve heard this before, but Alice in Zombieland has very little to do with Lewis Carroll’s classic. In fact, aside from the title itself and the white rabbit-shaped cloud that warns our Ali of danger, there’s nothing connecting the two. As someone who stays as far away from retellings as possible, I was overjoyed when I discovered this, but if you go into this expecting a new version of <i>that</i> story, you might find yourself disappointed.<br/><br/>Alice in Zombieland is, above all, a fun little bo</span>
  <span id="freeText3560949713556867705" style="display:none">I’m sure you’ve heard this before, but Alice in Zombieland has very little to do with Lewis Carroll’s classic. In fact, aside from the title itself and the white rabbit-shaped cloud that warns our Ali of danger, there’s nothing connecting the two. As someone who stays as far away from retellings as possible, I was overjoyed when I discovered this, but if you go into this expecting a new version of <i>that</i> story, you might find yourself disappointed.<br><br>Alice in Zombieland is, above all, a fun little book suitable for younger audience. While there are plenty of hot scenes and sexual references in there to contradict what I just wrote, the overall story lacks enough substance and depth to satisfy a more mature reader. This is mostly due to formulaic narrative and stock characters. That’s not to say, however, that this book is not worth reading – it is, as it has several things going for it, but it’s not nearly as original or exciting as I’d hoped.<br><br>The story is all too familiar: Ali’s entire family dies in a car accident caused by her schizophrenic father who was trying to save them from invisible monsters. After the tragedy, Ali goes to live with her grandparents, where she soon discovers that her father wasn’t nearly as crazy as he sounded. Monsters start popping up everywhere, but with them comes a group of young people led by the scorching hot Cole Holland, all of them trained to kill the zombies and defend humanity. <br><br>Although I liked Cole well enough, he didn’t even come close to provoking the reaction Showalter was going for. All the ingredients were there: the initial rudeness, the mystery surrounding him, the incredibly attractive looks, overprotectiveness, strength and impressive fighting skills, but I just never felt truly enthralled by him, not for a split second. It’s probably because, as a love interest, he seemed just a bit too plastic. Take this quote for example:<br><br><b>
  <i>I knew he was strong, determined, protective, and that he cared about his friends more than he cared about himself. He obeyed no rules but his own. In the Wild West days, he would have been an outlaw.</i>
</b><br><br>It’s true, Cole is all those things, which makes him exactly like hundreds of other characters that showed up recently. I’ve seen authors work with this mold and still manage to create something unique, be it through the sense of humor or something else entirely. But Showalter just didn’t succeed in making Cole memorable at all. <br><br>Where she failed with him, she succeeded with Alice… at least up to a point. Alice is also a stock character, but unlike with Cole, Gena Showalter managed to breathe some true spirit into her, which is why she’s the only thing I’m sure I’ll remember about this book. <br><br>Oddly enough, Showalter’s take on zombies was the most original thing about Alice in Zombieland, and my favorite part, to be honest. Existing only in the spirit realm, they cannot be seen or touched by just anyone, but that doesn’t mean they can’t do real harm. In order to fight them, Cole and the gang have to separate their spirits from their bodies, and it’s the first thing Ali had to learn as well. While I’m usually a blood-and-gore kinda gal, I found it all very interesting, although a bit confusing at times.<br><br>All in all, Alice in Zombieland is a fun, but rather unmemorable book that, I fear, was written merely to satisfy the market, and not in a creative outburst of any sort. A lot of adult authors are deciding to write YA these days because, let’s be honest, that’s where the money is, but some manage better than others, and Gena Showalter falls somewhere around the middle.<br><br>Do I think this book is worth reading? Definitely, if you’re looking for a compelling, fun read you’re likely to forget in a short while. There are times when a reader needs exactly that.<br><br><a href="http://www.thenocturnallibrary.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380226536i/681142.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="3560949713556867705" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1436762068" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1436762068" />
    <a title="Mizuki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki"><img alt="Mizuki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368277474p2/16842102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1436762068?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mizuki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mizuki" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki">Mizuki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=chinese-translation">chinese-translation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=no-hell-no">no-hell-no</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=disappointment">disappointment</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=are-you-kidding-me">are-you-kidding-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=one-of-the-worst-books-ever">one-of-the-worst-books-ever</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=mary-sue-warning">mary-sue-warning</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=young-adult-books">young-adult-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=bad-bad-bad-romance">bad-bad-bad-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=over-my-dead-body">over-my-dead-body</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=i-hate-love-triangle">i-hate-love-triangle</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1436762068" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16154184145212761931"><i>Reading Progress:</i><br/><br/>This is how I reacted to this book:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1445003133ra/16586150.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>(Link: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://sammo6661deth.deviantart.com/art/CHIBA-abuse-127149731'>http://sammo6661deth.deviantart.com/a...</a>)<br/><br/>Actually review here:<br/><br/><b>Note: I read the translated version of this book.</b><br/><br/>There is one word I think is the most suitable for this supposed Alice in Wonderland retelling, and this word is <b>ridiculous</b>.<br/><br/>(1) Calling this book an Alice-retelling is equated to lying. All of the Alice-references are so poorly done and senseless (a bunch of teenagers throwing a regular beer-and-disco-music party is equated to t</span>
  <span id="freeText16154184145212761931" style="display:none"><i>Reading Progress:</i><br><br>This is how I reacted to this book:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1445003133ra/16586150.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(Link: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://sammo6661deth.deviantart.com/art/CHIBA-abuse-127149731">http://sammo6661deth.deviantart.com/a...</a>)<br><br>Actually review here:<br><br><b>Note: I read the translated version of this book.</b><br><br>There is one word I think is the most suitable for this supposed Alice in Wonderland retelling, and this word is <b>ridiculous</b>.<br><br>(1) Calling this book an Alice-retelling is equated to lying. All of the Alice-references are so poorly done and senseless (a bunch of teenagers throwing a regular beer-and-disco-music party is equated to the Mad Tea Party, great isn't it?) it feels more like an insult to the original text than a respectful homage.<br><br>(2) This book is more about stupid teenage high school drama and over-the-top love triangles than Alice. I'm not kidding.<br><br>(3) The heroine Alice (aka Ali) spends a lot of time drooling over the masculine bad boy love interest Cole and fantasizing about making out with him (again I'm not kidding) than grieving over her dead family and worrying about the crisis of zombies going around eating people for dinner.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1447218529ra/16972851.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(Link: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://vampirekiki.deviantart.com/art/YOMI-abuse-137598903">http://vampirekiki.deviantart.com/art...</a>)<br><br>(4) As to the zombies....they only have spiritual forms and they are 'eating' the goodness in people then in turn making them zombies too. Why would they do this? <b>Because they are evil.</b> Not because they are hungry or need human flesh to keep their bodies functional. <br><br>Zombies with no physical forms? Zombies who eat people because they are evil!? Then why would those creatures be zombies at all? Why don't call those creatures 'phantoms' or 'wraiths' instead? Is the author so eager to ride the success of the recent zombie hyper, e.g. The Walking Dead and all those zombie movies out there?<br><br>(5) All the bullshit about Christianity and God and Good vs. Evil<br><br>I know, the heroine and her family are Christians, but must she keep talking nonsense about God so very often? I mean, do real-life Christians talk like this? It's so annoying. <br><br>To make thing worse, even Christian rock bands get mentions here and there. *facepalms*<br><br>And the nonsense about how the war between zombies and people who can 'see' them is the epic Good vs. Evil battle is also annoying as hell. <br><br>(6) The basic concepts about man-eating monsters and people who fought them could have worked out just fine <b>if the author actually has some basic writing skill and style to save her life.</b> But she doesn't, so the entire story turns out to be very flat, toneless and fake. The heroine lost her entire family? Monsters stalking her and wanting to eat people? I never felt worry about her and her friends, the writing is just that bad.<br><br>(7) Last but not least, the heroine's dear dead mother taught her teenage daughter that her virginity is a gift when the good woman was alive.<br><br>Okay, I'm alright with the 'don't do it when you are not ready and certain' message, but what the actual fuck about this 'virginity is a gift/valuable' BS? It's just downright backward and sexist. Have you ever heard a guy's virginity is a gift before? No? Like never? Now can you see what I mean?</span>
  <a data-text-id="16154184145212761931" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_976090316" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/976090316" />
    <a title="Ash" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9871824-ash"><img alt="Ash" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600418979p2/9871824.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/976090316?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ash" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ash" href="/user/show/9871824-ash">Ash</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer976090316" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15229505158907601225"><b>This book was so fun!!!!</b><br/><blockquote>
  <i>“Never forget that evil is evil. You cannot change it. You cannot lead it to the light. But, if you let it, evil can lead you to the darkness.” </i>
</blockquote><br/>I loved this book, surprisingly. I was really hesitant and I had actually decided to not read it some time ago, but back in August I noticed my BFF Lauren wanted to read it and I thought it would be fun to read together...<b>WELL</b>, we finally got to it, and I enjoyed it immensely!<br/><br/>The last "Alice and Wonderland" retelling I read wa</span>
  <span id="freeText15229505158907601225" style="display:none"><b>This book was so fun!!!!</b><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Never forget that evil is evil. You cannot change it. You cannot lead it to the light. But, if you let it, evil can lead you to the darkness.” </i>
</blockquote><br />I loved this book, surprisingly. I was really hesitant and I had actually decided to not read it some time ago, but back in August I noticed my BFF Lauren wanted to read it and I thought it would be fun to read together...<b>WELL</b>, we finally got to it, and I enjoyed it immensely!<br /><br />The last "Alice and Wonderland" retelling I read was...not good. I didn't enjoy it all that much - It turned me off to this book...but when L said she wanted to get to it this month, I was very much on board. I am happy to report that there wasn't much of an Alice in WONDERland vibe. If this is supposed to be a 'retelling' of sorts, its an incredibly loose retelling. <br /><br />I loved the characters <b>[Mostly Cole...always Cole]</b>. I'd seen the name <i>Cole Holland</i> on my GR feed numerous times, but I had no idea from which book he came.....<b>I DO NOW!!!</b> As soon as I saw his full name, I was excited to get to know him. He's great. Love, Love, Love! ALICE....I loved and hated her, but overall, I mostly loved her. She was sassy, and a fighter, I could definitely see us being friends! <i>[Especially when her best friend Kat, somewhat reminds me of myself]</i>. But, she rushed into things, and in doing so, acted quite stupidly at times. The other characters.....You either love or hate them. I found her Grandparents to me the most amusing of characters. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[so when her grandfather was turned, I was beyond heartbroken for her. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>THE ZOMBIES:</b> Obviously that isn't a spoiler, because...HELLO, its in the name. I won't go into detail, but I will definitely say that the way the author went about it, has got to be one of the most original ideas when it comes to the monsters. <br /><br />As tragic as I found the beginning to be....I didn't really think much on how the book as a whole would turn out. I knew it'd be full of bad ass fighting, and infatuations, and humor...but I didn't think it would also have so many more heartbreaking moments. No details...but I will say, that the fact that I wanted to cry...makes me love this book all the more. <b>I absolutely love</b> when a book can make me feel the characters emotions. It says a lot about the writing style, and I can totally say I loved it here. <br /><br />The ending of this book made me want to jump right into book two. UNFORTUNATELY, that won't be happening....but I <b>did</b> order books two and three before I was even halfway through this one. *Excitement*<br /><br /><i>come find me:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.facebook.com/ReadsAsh">www.facebook.com/ReadsAsh</a><br /><b>IG:</b> ash.reads <b>Twitter:</b> @ReadsAsh</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="15229505158907601225" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_351443329" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/351443329" />
    <a title="Donna {Book Passion For Life}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3024878-donna-book-passion-for-life"><img alt="Donna {Book Passion For Life}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563622982p2/3024878.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/351443329?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Donna {Book Passion For Life}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Donna {Book Passion For Life}" href="/user/show/3024878-donna-book-passion-for-life">Donna {Book Passion For Life}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781848451575" href="/book/show/15744840-alice-in-zombieland">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024878-donna-book-passion-for-life?shelf=for-review">for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024878-donna-book-passion-for-life?shelf=ya-dystopian-scifi-thriller">ya-dystopian-scifi-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer351443329" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8693252556720614193"><b>“Let’s see what I can do to change that, shall we? We’re going on a little adventure, you and I. When I give an order, you’ll obey it. There will be no asking politely, no matter how much you bat your lashes at me.” <br/><br/>4.5 stars</b><br/><br/>Where do I start with <i>Alice in Zombieland</i>....well, to be honest zombies are really not my thing AT ALL! I've read several zombie books and just cant see what all the hype is about - they just don't do anything for me, but because of all the awesome reviews on this book, I wa</span>
  <span id="freeText8693252556720614193" style="display:none"><b>“Let’s see what I can do to change that, shall we? We’re going on a little adventure, you and I. When I give an order, you’ll obey it. There will be no asking politely, no matter how much you bat your lashes at me.” <br /><br />4.5 stars</b><br /><br />Where do I start with <i>Alice in Zombieland</i>....well, to be honest zombies are really not my thing AT ALL! I've read several zombie books and just cant see what all the hype is about - they just don't do anything for me, but because of all the awesome reviews on this book, I wanted to give it go and yes, it's official.... Gena Showalter has convinced me that this zombie book RULES and I just want more and more of this amazing and unique world. <br /><br /><i>Alice in Zombieland</i> is a fun filled adrenaline ride, full of thrilling, engaging and explosive scenes and I really loved every minute of it. Gena Showalter really delivers in her excellent storytelling and gives us readers little signs of the original Alice in Wonderland. I have to say, I love the original story and I really enjoyed trying to spot them out in this book. I just wanted to try and unravel what each sign meant, especially the rabbit in the sky. It was a very intruiging twist but what I enjoyed about this novel so much is that it screams UNIQUENESS. The zombies in this story aren't just you're regular walking dead but there something different, and no, I'm not telling you and spoiling it for you, so I guess you're going to have to read the book for yourself but trust me what I say you won't be disappointed. This is why I enjoyed this book so much more to other zombie books...so yay! <br /><br />Now, the characters.....I need to talk about Cole first. *SIGH* I love him. He's just....wow. He literraly takes my breath away, he's that amazing. It was interesting to see why he is the way he is, he's broody and moody and people are scared of him but they have every right to be. He's the top slayer and he'll do anything to protect those he cares about. Now Alice, she's such a likable girl from page one, even through her losing her parents she tries to remain strong but it's not until she meets Cole that she really finds out what's going on. That her father was right...zombies are real and their after her. Another interesting part of this book was following Cole and Alice's romance, there's something very special that gives them a very deep connection, and even though we still don't know why this is, it still gives me hope that these two troubled characters can survive the battles and still remain in love. I'm very eager to see what happens with them. <br /><br />So if you're a fan of superb storytelling, excellent and interesting characters, with a romance that you will root for and a captivating story, then this is the book for you. Gena Showalters give a whole new meaning to zombies and I can't wait to see what she has in store for us next. <br /><br /><b>A big thank you to Mira Ink for giving me the opportunity to review this book.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="8693252556720614193" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1861190457" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1861190457" />
    <a title="Hannah G" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58220052-hannah-g"><img alt="Hannah G" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572171704p2/58220052.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1861190457?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hannah G" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hannah G" href="/user/show/58220052-hannah-g">Hannah G</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>
